### Round 1 | planner | planner_initial

- diagnosis: The task is to assess the likely AIE mechanism for a large neutral C56H46O2 molecule. The current working top1 is TICT, with ICT as top2. A third still-credible portfolio member is neutral aromatic. TICT leads because the scaffold contains many phenyl rotors, substantial branching, and a classic highly substituted multi-aryl alkene architecture where excited-state deactivation and AIE can be strongly tied to torsional motion. However, top1 is only provisional because the donor-acceptor pattern is not obviously strong enough to assume a pronounced twisted charge-transfer state without screening, and the same gross structure could also behave as a predominantly neutral aromatic emitter whose AIE mainly reflects restriction of intramolecular motions. Shared prepared structure context is available, which is useful for bounded geometry-aware tasks. Macro can screen one deterministic structural evidence family at a time, but it cannot decide the global mechanism. Microscopic can do one low-cost baseline S0/S1 action on the shared structure, which can provide indirect excited-state character cues, but it cannot in this first round do conformer sensitivity, torsion scans, or a multi-step mechanistic workflow. Because both topology-level and baseline electronic evidence are needed to separate TICT from ICT and neutral aromatic, the first round should gather both macro and microscopic evidence. The case remains in portfolio screening rather than pairwise contraction because a still-credible third candidate, neutral aromatic, has not yet been explicitly screened.

- action: macro_and_microscopic

- confidence: 0.45

- task_instruction: Run one bounded macro structural screen and one bounded microscopic baseline S0/S1 screen to reduce uncertainty among TICT, ICT, and neutral aromatic without making final mechanism claims.

This involves analyzing the molecule's rotor density, distribution of torsion candidates, and branching/peripheral rotor concentration to assess whether the structural features support a twisted intramolecular charge transfer (TICT) mechanism over a neutral aromatic interpretation.

The shared prepared structure context is available and will be leveraged to extract detailed rotor topology and torsion candidate summaries. This evidence will help clarify if the molecule's topology is unusually supportive of TICT relative to a simpler neutral aromatic explanation.
